     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Fightin%27_Texas_Aggie_Band" title="Fightin' Texas Aggie Band">Fightin' Texas Aggie Band</a>, the world's largest precision <a href="/wiki/Military_band" title="Military band">military</a> <a href="/wiki/Marching_band" title="Marching band">marching band</a>, provides music for University functions and presents intricate halftime performances at football games.<sup id="cite_ref-CorpsAbout_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CorpsAbout-129"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Some band drills are so complicated that they require band members to step between each other's feet to complete the maneuvers.<sup id="cite_ref-steponfeet_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steponfeet-131"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> These drills must be drawn by hand as computer marching programs have returned errors; their calculations require two people to be in the same spot at the same time.<sup id="cite_ref-errorband_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-errorband-132"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Activities">Activities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_A%26M_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Activities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:TAMUsingingcadets.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1b/TAMUsingingcadets.jpg/220px-TAMUsingingcadets.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1b/TAMUsingingcadets.jpg/330px-TAMUsingingcadets.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1b/TAMUsingingcadets.jpg/440px-TAMUsingingcadets.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:TAMUsingingcadets.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Texas A&amp;M University Singing Cadets
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Texas A&amp;M has over 800 student organizations, including academic, service, religious, <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities" class="mw-redirect">Greek</a>, and common interest organizations. Orientation programs encourage students to become involved in campus activities and organizations from the beginning.<sup id="cite_ref-newsletter2003_12_4_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsletter2003_12_4-133"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> An April 2005 campus survey found that 74% of the students were currently involved with at least one organization and that 88% participated in a campus organization in the past.<sup id="cite_ref-studentinvolvement_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-studentinvolvement-134"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>One of the oldest student organizations is the <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_Singing_Cadets" title="Texas A&amp;M Singing Cadets">Singing Cadets</a>, founded in 1893. Known as the &quot;Voice of Aggieland&quot;, the Singing Cadets are an all-male choral group with about 70 members not affiliated with the Corps of Cadets. The group travels nationally and has completed several international tours; most recently, South Africa in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-singingcadets_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singingcadets-135"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_Hillel" title="Texas A&amp;M Hillel">Texas A&amp;M Hillel</a>, the oldest Hillel organization in the United States, was founded in 1920 at the original college. The organization occurred three years before the national <a href="/wiki/Hillel_Foundation" title="Hillel Foundation" class="mw-redirect">Hillel Foundation</a> was organized at <a href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois" title="University of Illinois" class="mw-redirect">University of Illinois</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hillel_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hillel-136"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hillel2_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hillel2-137"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:TAMU_Rec2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/TAMU_Rec2.JPG/220px-TAMU_Rec2.JPG" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/TAMU_Rec2.JPG/330px-TAMU_Rec2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/TAMU_Rec2.JPG/440px-TAMU_Rec2.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:TAMU_Rec2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Student Rec Center
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/GLBT_Aggies" title="GLBT Aggies">GLBT Aggies</a> is the descendant organization of Gay Student Services (GSS), the only student organization to ever successfully sue the institution for official recognition.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> In the decision <a href="/wiki/Gay_Student_Services_v._Texas_A%26M_University" title="Gay Student Services v. Texas A&amp;M University">Gay Student Services v. Texas A&amp;M University</a> the <a href="/wiki/Fifth_U.S._Circuit_Court_of_Appeals" title="Fifth U.S. Circuit Court of Appeals" class="mw-redirect">Fifth U.S. Circuit Court of Appeals</a> held that the <a href="/wiki/First_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="First Amendment to the United States Constitution">First Amendment</a> required public universities to recognize student organizations aimed at gay students.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Graduate Student Council, founded in 1995, serves as the student government for Texas A&amp;M University?s graduate and professional students. It is a council representing all TAMU graduate students with a purpose to improve graduate students? academic, living and social experiences. The GSC represents student?s concerns and is their liaison with the University Administration.<sup id="cite_ref-GSC_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GSC-140"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Students exercise at the Student Rec Center, a three-story facility encompassing 373,000 square feet (34,650&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>), which includes exercise equipment, athletic courts, an indoor running track, a rock-climbing tower, and one of the top competitive pools and diving wells in America. The Rec Center also organizes intramural sports throughout the year.<sup id="cite_ref-reccenter_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reccenter-141"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Some national service organizations originated at A&amp;M. Aggie students founded the largest one-day student-run service project in America known as The Big Event. The annual service project allows students to give back to their community by assisting local residents.<sup id="cite_ref-bigevent_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bigevent-142"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> The organization CARPOOL, a student run, <a href="/wiki/Designated_driver" title="Designated driver">safe ride program</a> has provided over 179,000&nbsp;free&nbsp;rides (as of January 2011) to Aggies unable to transport themselves home. Its organizers also assist other universities in establishing similar programs.<sup id="cite_ref-Carpool1_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carpool1-143"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-carpool3_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carpool3-144"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, the <a href="/wiki/Corporation_for_National_and_Community_Service" title="Corporation for National and Community Service">Corporation for National and Community Service</a> listed A&amp;M among the 500 academic institutions in the 2005?06 President's Higher Education Community Service Honor Roll.<sup id="cite_ref-honorroll_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-honorroll-145"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Student Government Association (SGA), one of A&amp;M's largest organizations, consists of over 1,300 student members in 3 branches, 15 committees, and 4 commissions. SGA has changed little since 1972, except its relative position within the official framework of the university.<sup id="cite_ref-StudentSenate_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StudentSenate-146"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_A%26M_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Princeton_Review" title="The Princeton Review">The Princeton Review</a></i> ranked <i><a href="/wiki/The_Battalion" title="The Battalion">The Battalion</a></i>, founded in 1893, as the 5th best college newspaper in America in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-battranking_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-battranking-147"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> Students also publish a secondary school newspaper, the <i>Maroon Weekly</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-maroonweekly_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maroonweekly-148"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i>Aggieland</i>, formerly known as <i>The Olio</i> and <i>The Longhorn</i>, is one of America's largest college yearbooks in number of pages and copies sold.<sup id="cite_ref-AgYearbook_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AgYearbook-149"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AgYearbook2_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AgYearbook2-150"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> The university houses the public broadcasting stations: <i><a href="/wiki/KAMU-TV" title="KAMU-TV">KAMU-TV</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/PBS" title="PBS">PBS</a> member station since 1970, <i><a href="/wiki/KAMU-FM" title="KAMU-FM">KAMU-FM</a></i> an <a href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" title="National Public Radio" class="mw-redirect">NPR</a> affiliate since 1977,<sup id="cite_ref-KBTXKAMUFM_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KBTXKAMUFM-151"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> and the student-run <i><a href="/wiki/KANM" title="KANM">KANM</a></i>, &quot;the college station of <a href="/wiki/College_Station,_Texas" title="College Station, Texas">College Station</a>&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-KANM_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KANM-152"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> W5AC broadcast the first live, play-by-play broadcast of a college football game, at Kyle Field, in November 1921. The game, played in Dallas between Aggies and <a href="/wiki/Texas_Longhorns" title="Texas Longhorns">University of Texas</a>, ended in a scoreless tie.<sup id="cite_ref-schultz_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schultz-153"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_A%26M_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Traditions_of_Texas_A%26M_University" title="Traditions of Texas A&amp;M University">Traditions of Texas A&amp;M University</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_Texas_A%26M_University_terms" title="Glossary of Texas A&amp;M University terms">Glossary of Texas A&amp;M University terms</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:AggieRing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Close-up of gold ring. On the top, the words Texas A&amp;M University 1876 encircle an eagle atop a shield over the numbers 0 and 4. The left side contains a large star and an oak. The right shows a cannon, saber, and rifle with the crossed flags of the United States and Texas." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/AggieRing.jpg/220px-AggieRing.jpg" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/AggieRing.jpg/330px-AggieRing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/4c/AggieRing.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:AggieRing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Aggie Ring for the class of 2004
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Texas A&amp;M culture is a product of the university's founding as a rural military and agricultural school. Although the school and surrounding community have grown, and military training is no longer required, the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Texas_A%26M_University" title="History of Texas A&amp;M University">school's history</a> has instilled in students &quot;the idealized elements of a small-town life: community, tradition, loyalty, optimism, and unabashed sentimentality.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-burka2000_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burka2000-154"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Texas_Monthly" title="Texas Monthly">Texas Monthly</a></i> posits that Texas A&amp;M students' respect for school traditions and values is the university's greatest strength.<sup id="cite_ref-burkaNov2006_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burkaNov2006-155"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> Some of the school traditions date to the 1890s, while others have been introduced more recently. These traditions help current and former students to cultivate the Aggie Spirit, a sense of loyalty and respect for the school.<sup id="cite_ref-tresaugue_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tresaugue-156"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> They dictate many aspects of student life, including how to greet others (using the official school greeting &quot;Howdy!&quot;),<sup id="cite_ref-hallett_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hallett-157"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> how to act at an A&amp;M sporting event, and, in many cases, what words a student may use in conversation.<sup id="cite_ref-gravois_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gravois-158"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The most visible tradition among seniors and former students is the wearing of the <a href="/wiki/Aggie_Ring" title="Aggie Ring" class="mw-redirect">Aggie Ring</a>, whose design has been relatively unchanged since its introduction in 1894.<sup id="cite_ref-kane_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kane-159"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> Students may order a ring after completing 90 <a href="/wiki/Credit_hours" title="Credit hours" class="mw-redirect">credit hours</a> of coursework, including at least 45 hours at A&amp;M, or after graduation. Graduate students may receive a ring after 75% of their graduate coursework is completed or after the acceptance of their dissertation or thesis.<sup id="cite_ref-ring2_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ring2-160"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> Though unsanctioned by the University, many students &quot;dunk&quot; their newly acquired Aggie Rings into a pitcher of beer and quickly chug the entire pitcher to &quot;earn&quot; the ring. Some students dunk their rings in alternative substances, including ice cream or nonalcoholic beverages.<sup id="cite_ref-ring3_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ring3-161"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:AggieMuster.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/AggieMuster.jpg/220px-AggieMuster.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/AggieMuster.jpg/330px-AggieMuster.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/AggieMuster.jpg/440px-AggieMuster.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:AggieMuster.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_University_Corps_of_Cadets#Ross_Volunteers" title="Texas A&amp;M University Corps of Cadets">Ross Volunteers</a> perform a rifleman's 
        <a href="/wiki/Salute" title="Salute">salute</a> as candles are lit for the deceased at the 2007 
        <a href="/wiki/Muster_(Texas_A%26M_University)" title="Muster (Texas A&amp;M University)">Aggie Muster</a> at 
        <a href="/wiki/Reed_Arena" title="Reed Arena">Reed Arena</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In keeping with the idea that all current and former students comprise a family, Aggies have created two traditions to honor members of the Aggie family who have died. <a href="/wiki/Muster_(Texas_A%26M_University)" title="Muster (Texas A&amp;M University)">Aggie Muster</a> is held annually on the anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_San_Jacinto" title="Battle of San Jacinto">Battle of San Jacinto</a>, April 21, to honor any current and former student who died during the previous year. Over 300 Musters are held around the world, with the largest taking place at <a href="/wiki/Reed_Arena" title="Reed Arena">Reed Arena</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_University_campus" title="Texas A&amp;M University campus" class="mw-redirect">Texas A&amp;M University campus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-lozano_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lozano-162"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> All Muster ceremonies feature the Roll Call for the Absent. As the names of the deceased Aggies are called, a family member or friend answers &quot;Here&quot; and lights a candle, to symbolize that although their loved one is not present in body, his or her spirit will shine forever.<sup id="cite_ref-lopez_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lopez-163"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-silvertaps_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-silvertaps-164"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> The event received worldwide attention during World War II, when 25 Aggies &quot;mustered&quot; during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Corregidor" title="Battle of Corregidor">battle</a> for the island of <a href="/wiki/Corregidor" title="Corregidor" class="mw-redirect">Corregidor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tutt_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tutt-165"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Students who die while enrolled at Texas A&amp;M are also honored at Silver Taps, a ceremony held, when necessary, on the first Tuesday of the month. This tradition began as a memorial for former Texas A&amp;M president <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Sullivan_Ross" title="Lawrence Sullivan Ross">Lawrence Sullivan Ross</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hegstrom_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hegstrom-166"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> On the day of the ceremony, flags fly half-staff and notices are posted throughout campus. At 10:15&nbsp;pm the lights around campus are extinguished and hymns chime from Albritton Tower while students and faculty collect in the Academic Plaza. Following a <a href="/wiki/21-gun_salute" title="21-gun salute">21-gun salute</a> by the Ross Volunteer Firing Squad, six <a href="/wiki/Bugle_(instrument)" title="Bugle (instrument)" class="mw-redirect">buglers</a> play an A&amp;M version of the song <i><a href="/wiki/Taps" title="Taps">Taps</a></i>, Silver Taps, three times from the dome of the school's Academic Building: once to the north, the south and to the west. The song is not played to the east symbolizing that the sun will never rise on that Aggie again.<sup id="cite_ref-silvertaps_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-silvertaps-164"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_A%26M_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:2007-SBF.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Large flames engulf the top layer of a circular three-tier structure of logs; the logs are vertical to the ground." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/2007-SBF.jpg/170px-2007-SBF.jpg" width="170" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/2007-SBF.jpg/255px-2007-SBF.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/2007-SBF.jpg/340px-2007-SBF.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:2007-SBF.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 2007 Student Bonfire
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="12th_Man">12th Man</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_A%26M_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 12th Man">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>Aggie <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">football</a> fans are called the <a href="/wiki/12th_Man_(football)" title="12th Man (football)" class="mw-redirect">12th Man</a>. The meaning is that they support the 11 players on the field and, moreover, are willing to enter the game if necessary. To further symbolize their &quot;readiness, desire, and enthusiasm,&quot; the entire student body stands throughout the game.<sup id="cite_ref-12thMan_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12thMan-167"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> The tradition began on January 2, 1922, at the <a href="/wiki/Dixie_Classic_(bowl_game)" title="Dixie Classic (bowl game)">Dixie Classic</a> where A&amp;M played <a href="/wiki/Centre_College" title="Centre College">Centre College</a>. A&amp;M had so many injuries in the first half of the game that <a href="/wiki/Head_coach" title="Head coach">Coach</a> <a href="/wiki/Dana_X._Bible" title="Dana X. Bible">Dana X. Bible</a> feared he wouldn?t have enough men to finish the game. He called into the stands for <a href="/wiki/E._King_Gill#History" title="E. King Gill" class="mw-redirect">E. King Gill</a>, a reserve who had left football after the regular season to play basketball. Although he did not actually play, his readiness symbolized the willingness of all Aggies to support their team to the point of actually entering the game. A&amp;M won 22?14, but E. King Gill was the only man left standing on the sidelines for the Aggies.<sup id="cite_ref-beano_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beano-168"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> In recent decades, the 12th Man is represented on the field by a <a href="/wiki/Walk-on_(sport_term)" title="Walk-on (sport term)" class="mw-redirect">walk-on</a> player who wears the No. 12 jersey and participates in kick-offs.<sup id="cite_ref-heater_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heater-169"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The 12th Man uses a variety of school yells, rather than cheers, to support Aggie teams. Each year the student body elects five students to serve as the Yell Leaders.<sup id="cite_ref-alvaradoyell_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alvaradoyell-170"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> At midnight before each home <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> game at Kyle Field or at a predesignated location at away games, the fans gather together to practice the yells for the next day's game.<sup id="cite_ref-hallett_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hallett-157"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-drehs_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drehs-171"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup> Led by the Yell Leaders, and the Fightin' Texas Aggie Band, the Twelfth Man files into the stadium to participate in <a href="/wiki/Midnight_Yell_Practice" title="Midnight Yell Practice">Midnight Yell Practice</a> to practice yells, sing the <a href="//en.wikisource.org/wiki/Aggie_War_Hymn" class="extiw" title="wikisource:Aggie War Hymn">War Hymn</a>, and joke about their opponents. At the conclusion of the yell practice, the stadium lights are extinguished and fans kiss their dates. This is also done as practice, because Aggies are expected to &quot;mug down&quot;, or kiss their dates, every time the football team scores on the field.<sup id="cite_ref-drehs_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drehs-171"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mugdown_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mugdown-172"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i> named Midnight Yell as one of the &quot;100 Things You Gotta Do Before You Graduate.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-si100_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-si100-173"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bonfire">Bonfire</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_A%26M_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Bonfire">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>Almost every year since 1909, A&amp;M students have built a large bonfire to celebrate their &quot;burning desire to beat the hell outta&quot; the University of Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-smith2007_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smith2007-174"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Aggie_Bonfire" title="Aggie Bonfire">Aggie Bonfire</a> was traditionally lit around <a href="/wiki/Thanksgiving" title="Thanksgiving">Thanksgiving</a> in conjunction with the festivities surrounding the annual <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">college football</a> game between the schools.<sup id="cite_ref-bernstein_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bernstein-175"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> Though it began as a trash pile,<sup id="cite_ref-as_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-as-176"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> Aggie Bonfire evolved into a massive six-tiered structure, the world record being held at 109 feet (30&nbsp;m).<sup id="cite_ref-bernstein_175-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bernstein-175"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WorldRec_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WorldRec-177"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup> After the collapse of the 1999 structure, causing the death of 11 students and one former student, the university suspended Bonfire indefinitely, but the tradition continues off-campus without direct University involvement, sanction, or participation.<sup id="cite_ref-milloy_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-milloy-178"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-badger_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-badger-179"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_A%26M_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_Aggies" title="Texas A&amp;M Aggies">Texas A&amp;M Aggies</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Texas_A%26M_University_aTm_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Texas_A%26M_University_aTm_logo.svg/220px-Texas_A%26M_University_aTm_logo.svg.png" width="220" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Texas_A%26M_University_aTm_logo.svg/330px-Texas_A%26M_University_aTm_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Texas_A%26M_University_aTm_logo.svg/440px-Texas_A%26M_University_aTm_logo.svg.png 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Texas_A%26M_University_aTm_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> TAMU logo
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Aggies are a member of the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference" title="Southeastern Conference">Southeastern Conference</a> in all sports as of July 1, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-swconference_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swconference-181"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> Previously a charter member of the <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Conference" title="Southwest Conference">Southwest Conference</a> until its dissolution in 1996, A&amp;M competed in the <a href="/wiki/Big_12_Conference" title="Big 12 Conference">Big 12 Conference</a> until June 30, 2012. The school's 20 sports teams are known as the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Aggie" title="Texas Aggie" class="mw-redirect">Aggies</a>, and the school's colors are maroon and white.<sup id="cite_ref-big12aggies_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-big12aggies-182"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup> As of April 2011, Aggies have earned 138 Southwest and Big 12 conference regular-season and tournament titles and 11 team national championships.<sup id="cite_ref-tamuathleticsfacts_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tamuathleticsfacts-183"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> The women's soccer team, formed in 1993, earned 15 consecutive NCAA Tournament appearances from 1995 to 2009, advancing at least as far as the round of 16 in seven of the last eight appearances.<sup id="cite_ref-soccerrecords_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soccerrecords-184"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup> The women's volleyball team earned 12 consecutive NCAA Tournament appearances from 1993 to 2004, advancing past the first round each time.<sup id="cite_ref-volleyballrecords_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-volleyballrecords-185"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-big12champs_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-big12champs-186"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2004 <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated_on_Campus" title="Sports Illustrated on Campus" class="mw-redirect">Sports Illustrated on Campus</a></i> ranked <a href="/wiki/Olsen_Field" title="Olsen Field" class="mw-redirect">Olsen Field</a> &quot;the best college baseball venue&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-Olsen_Field_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olsen_Field-187"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i> ranked the university 46th, in a 2002 analysis of &quot;America's Best Sports College[s]&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-bestsports_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bestsports-188"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup> and College Station the 9th best college sports town.<sup id="cite_ref-FBWeekend_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FBWeekend-189"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>A&amp;M's <a href="/wiki/College_rivalry" title="College rivalry">archrival</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Longhorns" title="Texas Longhorns">University of Texas</a>. In 2004, sporting events between the Aggies and Longhorns became known as the <a href="/wiki/Lone_Star_Showdown" title="Lone Star Showdown" class="mw-redirect">Lone Star Showdown</a>. The most-watched event in the rivalry is the annual <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> game held the day of <a href="/wiki/Thanksgiving_(United_States)" title="Thanksgiving (United States)">Thanksgiving</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fridayfootball_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fridayfootball-190"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-recordcrowd_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recordcrowd-191"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> Other rivalries include <a href="/wiki/Texas_Tech_Red_Raiders" title="Texas Tech Red Raiders" class="mw-redirect">Texas Tech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Brazos" title="Battle of the Brazos">Baylor University</a>, and the recently renewed rivalries with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Arkansas" title="University of Arkansas">University of Arkansas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_State_University" title="Louisiana State University">Louisiana State University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dirocco_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dirocco-192"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-griffin_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-griffin-193"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Techrival_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Techrival-194"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-arkrival_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arkrival-195"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_A%26M_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Kyle_Field_Montana_State_vs_A%26M_Sept_1_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Kyle_Field_Montana_State_vs_A%26M_Sept_1_2007.jpg/220px-Kyle_Field_Montana_State_vs_A%26M_Sept_1_2007.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Kyle_Field_Montana_State_vs_A%26M_Sept_1_2007.jpg/330px-Kyle_Field_Montana_State_vs_A%26M_Sept_1_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Kyle_Field_Montana_State_vs_A%26M_Sept_1_2007.jpg/440px-Kyle_Field_Montana_State_vs_A%26M_Sept_1_2007.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Kyle_Field_Montana_State_vs_A%26M_Sept_1_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A view from the student section of Kyle Field during a 2007 football game
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_Aggies_football" title="Texas A&amp;M Aggies football">Texas A&amp;M Aggies football</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Founded in 1894, the <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> team has won 18 Southwest Conference championships, 3 Big 12 South Division championships, 1 Big 12 championship, and 1 national championship.<sup id="cite_ref-FootballChampHist_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FootballChampHist-196"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup> The team has appeared in 30 <a href="/wiki/Bowl_games" title="Bowl games" class="mw-redirect">bowl games</a>, winning 13,<sup id="cite_ref-bowlhistory_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlhistory-197"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup> and has produced 41 first Team All-Americans, 5 Academic All-Americans, and 2 <a href="/wiki/Heisman_Trophy" title="Heisman Trophy">Heisman Trophy</a> winners, <a href="/wiki/John_David_Crow" title="John David Crow">John David Crow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Manziel" title="Johnny Manziel">Johnny Manziel</a>, in 1957 and 2012 respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-footballhis60_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footballhis60-198"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup> Twenty-one Aggies currently play in the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nflaggieplayers_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nflaggieplayers-199"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NFLAgs_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NFLAgs-200"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Since 1904, home football games have been played at <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Field" title="Kyle Field">Kyle Field</a>, a stadium with a current capacity of 83,002.<sup id="cite_ref-KF_Attendance_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KF_Attendance-201"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2004, <i><a href="/wiki/CBS_SportsLine.com" title="CBS SportsLine.com" class="mw-redirect">CBS SportsLine.com</a></i> ranked Kyle Field the top football stadium while <i><a href="/wiki/Sporting_News" title="Sporting News">Sporting News</a></i> ranked it fourth.<sup id="cite_ref-Kyle_Field_CBS_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kyle_Field_CBS-202"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sporting_News_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sporting_News-203"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup> The same year <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated_on_Campus" title="Sports Illustrated on Campus" class="mw-redirect">Sports Illustrated on Campus</a></i> ranked an A&amp;M football weekend the third best college football experience.<sup id="cite_ref-FBWeekend2_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FBWeekend2-204"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">Basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_A%26M_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Basketball">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Lss_2008_bb_damion_james.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Lss_2008_bb_damion_james.jpg/220px-Lss_2008_bb_damion_james.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Lss_2008_bb_damion_james.jpg/330px-Lss_2008_bb_damion_james.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Lss_2008_bb_damion_james.jpg/440px-Lss_2008_bb_damion_james.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Lss_2008_bb_damion_james.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A men's basketball game at Reed Arena in January 2008
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_Aggies_men%27s_basketball" title="Texas A&amp;M Aggies men's basketball">Texas A&amp;M Aggies men's basketball</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_Aggies_women%27s_basketball" title="Texas A&amp;M Aggies women's basketball">Texas A&amp;M Aggies women's basketball</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Founded in 1912, the men's basketball team won 11 Southwest Conference championships and 2 Southwest Conference Tournament championships. The team has appeared in the <a href="/wiki/National_Invitation_Tournament" title="National Invitation Tournament">National Invitation Tournament</a> 6 times and in the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA Tournament</a> 11 times, of which 3 resulted in <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">Sweet Sixteen</a> appearances, the highest round to which the Aggies have advanced.<sup id="cite_ref-AgBballHist_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AgBballHist-205"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup> The women's basketball team has 1 Southwest Conference Tournament championship,1 regular season Big 12 Conference championship and 2 Big 12 Tournament championships, most recently in 2011. The women have advanced to 8 NCAA Tournament appearances, winning the National Championship in 2011. They have also competed in the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_National_Invitation_Tournament" title="Women's National Invitation Tournament">WNIT</a> twice, winning that tournament in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-womenbb_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-womenbb-206"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The men's basketball team was coached by head coach <a href="/wiki/Mark_Turgeon" title="Mark Turgeon">Mark Turgeon</a> for four years until he left for the head coaching position at the <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Terrapins_men%27s_basketball" title="Maryland Terrapins men's basketball">University of Maryland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Turgeon_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turgeon-207"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup> The current head basketball coach is <a href="/wiki/Billy_Kennedy_(basketball)" title="Billy Kennedy (basketball)">Billy Kennedy</a>; he is entering his second season and leading the Aggies into the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference" title="Southeastern Conference">Southeastern Conference</a>. The women's team has been coached by <a href="/wiki/Gary_Blair" title="Gary Blair">Gary Blair</a> since 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-dickpatrick_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dickpatrick-208"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup> Home games are played at the 12,989-seat <a href="/wiki/Reed_Arena" title="Reed Arena">Reed Arena</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-reedarena_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reedarena-209"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/G._Rollie_White_Coliseum" title="G. Rollie White Coliseum">G. Rollie White Coliseum</a>, formerly the home of the volleyball and basketball teams, hosted basketball games before Reed Arena opened in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-grollie_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grollie-210"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_A%26M_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Texas_A%26M_University_people" title="List of Texas A&amp;M University people">List of Texas A&amp;M University people</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:TAMU_FormerStudents1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/TAMU_FormerStudents1.JPG/220px-TAMU_FormerStudents1.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/TAMU_FormerStudents1.JPG/330px-TAMU_FormerStudents1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/TAMU_FormerStudents1.JPG/440px-TAMU_FormerStudents1.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:TAMU_FormerStudents1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Clayton_Williams" title="Clayton Williams">Clayton W. Williams, Jr.</a>, Alumni Center is the home of 
        <a href="/wiki/The_Association_of_Former_Students" title="The Association of Former Students">The Association of Former Students</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Horace_S._Carswell,_Jr._MOH.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/38/Horace_S._Carswell%2C_Jr._MOH.JPG/170px-Horace_S._Carswell%2C_Jr._MOH.JPG" width="170" height="284" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/38/Horace_S._Carswell%2C_Jr._MOH.JPG/255px-Horace_S._Carswell%2C_Jr._MOH.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/38/Horace_S._Carswell%2C_Jr._MOH.JPG/340px-Horace_S._Carswell%2C_Jr._MOH.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Horace_S._Carswell,_Jr._MOH.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Specimen 
        <a href="/wiki/Medal_of_Honor" title="Medal of Honor">Medals of Honor</a> were on display at the Memorial Student Center (MSC) on the Texas A&amp;M campus for each of the University's seven recipients, including Horace S. Carswell's medal (pictured above). The medals are temporarily on display in Rudder Tower during renovation of the MSC.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>With over 280,000 former students,<sup id="cite_ref-academicfacts_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-academicfacts-211"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup> A&amp;M has one of the largest and most active <a href="/wiki/The_Association_of_Former_Students" title="The Association of Former Students">alumni groups</a> in America. Many Aggies have attained local, national, and international prominence.<sup id="cite_ref-TAMU_Facts_World_Impact_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TAMU_Facts_World_Impact-212"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Quiroga" title="Jorge Quiroga">Jorge Quiroga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martin_Torrijos" title="Martin Torrijos" class="mw-redirect">Martin Torrijos</a> have served as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">heads of state</a> for <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>, respectively, and <a href="/wiki/Rick_Perry" title="Rick Perry">Rick Perry</a> is the current <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Texas" title="Governor of Texas">Governor of Texas</a> and 2012 US Presidential candidate. Robert Gates, Secretary of Defense in the George W. Bush and Obama administrations,is a past president of the university. Congressmen <a href="/wiki/Joe_Barton" title="Joe Barton">Joe Barton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Flores" title="Bill Flores">Bill Flores</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeb_Hensarling" title="Jeb Hensarling">Jeb Hensarling</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Louie_Gohmert" title="Louie Gohmert">Louie Gohmert</a>, and former Austin, Texas, mayor <a href="/wiki/Will_Wynn" title="Will Wynn">Will Wynn</a> are all graduates.<sup id="cite_ref-formerstudentachievements_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-formerstudentachievements-213"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Aggies made their mark on the <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">gridiron</a> with <a href="/wiki/Houston_Texans" title="Houston Texans">Houston Texans</a> head coach <a href="/wiki/Gary_Kubiak" title="Gary Kubiak">Gary Kubiak</a>, title-winning coach <a href="/wiki/Gene_Stallings" title="Gene Stallings">Gene Stallings</a>, Oakland Raiders head coach <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Allen_(American_football)" title="Dennis Allen (American football)">Dennis Allen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Houston_Oilers" title="Houston Oilers" class="mw-redirect">Houston Oilers</a> defensive tackle <a href="/wiki/Ray_Childress" title="Ray Childress">Ray Childress</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heisman_Trophy" title="Heisman Trophy">Heisman Trophy</a> winners <a href="/wiki/John_David_Crow" title="John David Crow">John David Crow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Manziel" title="Johnny Manziel">Johnny Manziel</a>, Heisman runner-up, legislator, and actor <a href="/wiki/John_Kimbrough" title="John Kimbrough">John Kimbrough</a>, punt returner <a href="/wiki/Dante_Hall" title="Dante Hall">Dante Hall</a>, offensive tackle <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Webb" title="Richmond Webb">Richmond Webb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Lions" title="Detroit Lions">Detroit Lions</a> defensive end and punter <a href="/wiki/Yale_Lary" title="Yale Lary">Yale Lary</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Cowboys" title="Dallas Cowboys">Dallas Cowboys</a> assistant coach and former player <a href="/wiki/Dat_Nguyen" title="Dat Nguyen">Dat Nguyen</a>, punter <a href="/wiki/Shane_Lechler" title="Shane Lechler">Shane Lechler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denver_Broncos" title="Denver Broncos">Denver Broncos</a> linebacker <a href="/wiki/Von_Miller" title="Von Miller">Von Miller</a>, and defensive end <a href="/wiki/Ty_Warren" title="Ty Warren">Ty Warren</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GeneStallings_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GeneStallings-214"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Famous_Ath_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous_Ath-215"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bear_Bryant" title="Bear Bryant">Paul &quot;Bear&quot; Bryant</a> coached at A&amp;M where &quot;survivors&quot; of his grueling football practice camp at <a href="/wiki/Junction,_Texas" title="Junction, Texas">Junction, Texas</a> were nicknamed named <a href="/wiki/The_Junction_Boys" title="The Junction Boys" class="mw-redirect">The Junction Boys</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-junction_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-junction-216"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-junction2_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-junction2-217"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup> Other famous Aggie athletes include <a href="/wiki/Randy_Barnes" title="Randy Barnes">Randy Barnes</a>, indoor/outdoor shotput world record holder, baseball standouts <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Knoblauch" title="Chuck Knoblauch">Chuck Knoblauch</a> and Wally Moon; along with <a href="/wiki/Stacy_Sykora" title="Stacy Sykora">Stacy Sykora</a>, Libero for the USA national volleyball team.<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_Ath_215-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous_Ath-215"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Aggies have also made a mark on <a href="/wiki/Pop_culture" title="Pop culture" class="mw-redirect">pop culture</a>. <a href="/wiki/Robert_Earl_Keen" title="Robert Earl Keen">Robert Earl Keen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lyle_Lovett" title="Lyle Lovett">Lyle Lovett</a>, who often strummed their guitars on the porch of their Northgate home, have become popular country singers.<sup id="cite_ref-RKeen_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RKeen-218"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/William_A._Pailes" title="William A. Pailes">William A. Pailes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_E._Fossum" title="Michael E. Fossum">Michael E. Fossum</a> became NASA astronauts.<sup id="cite_ref-geller_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geller-219"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rip_Torn" title="Rip Torn">Rip Torn</a> is a veteran of the <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_States" title="Cinema of the United States">silver screen</a><sup id="cite_ref-Famous_Ath_215-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous_Ath-215"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Neal_Boortz" title="Neal Boortz">Neal Boortz</a> is a nationally syndicated talk show host with the sixth largest listening audience in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-NBoortz_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NBoortz-220"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Radio2_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Radio2-221"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wen_Ho_Lee" title="Wen Ho Lee">Wen Ho Lee</a>, a doctoral graduate of A&amp;M, became the subject of a 1999 espionage investigation; though arrested, charges were dropped in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-WenLee_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WenLee-222"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Many Aggies have become business leaders, particularly in the fields of energy, construction, communications, and chemistry. Current leaders include Ellis Field namesake Mark Ellis, President, Chairman, and CEO of Linn Energy, Jack Whiteside, President of Barnes &amp; Click, Inc.;<sup id="cite_ref-JackWhiteside_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JackWhiteside-223"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lowry_Mays" title="Lowry Mays">Lowry Mays</a>, chairman and CEO of Clear Channel Communications;<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_Ath_215-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous_Ath-215"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/George_P._Mitchell" title="George P. Mitchell">George P. Mitchell</a>, chairman and CEO, Mitchell Energy and Development Corp.;<sup id="cite_ref-formerstudentachievements_213-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-formerstudentachievements-213"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> H. B. Zachry, President of the H.B. Zachry Company; John Zachry, CEO of Zachry Corp.; David Zachry, President of Zachry Corp.;<sup id="cite_ref-Zachry_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zachry-224"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Khalid_A._Al-Falih" title="Khalid A. Al-Falih">Khalid A. Al-Falih</a>, President and CEO of Saudi Aramco;<sup id="cite_ref-Al-Falih_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Al-Falih-225"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup> Stephen M. Johnson, Chairman, President and CEO of McDermott International, Inc. and <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Castro-Wright" title="Eduardo Castro-Wright">Eduardo Castro-Wright</a>, CEO of Wal-Mart Stores USA.<sup id="cite_ref-EWright_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EWright-226"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Because of A&amp;M's military roots, many Aggies have become leaders in the armed forces, and were featured in the 1943 propaganda film <i><a href="/wiki/We%27ve_Never_Been_Licked" title="We've Never Been Licked">We've Never Been Licked</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-neverbeenlicked_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neverbeenlicked-227"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/George_H._Gay,_Jr." title="George H. Gay, Jr.">George H. Gay, Jr.</a>, was the sole survivor of Torpedo Squadron 8 in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Midway" title="Battle of Midway">Battle of Midway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gay_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gay-228"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup> Lieutenant General <a href="/wiki/Jay_T._Robbins" title="Jay T. Robbins">Jay T. Robbins</a> became a fighter ace in World War II with 22 aerial victories.<sup id="cite_ref-JayRobbins_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JayRobbins-229"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> Major General <a href="/wiki/Robert_B._Williams" title="Robert B. Williams">Robert B. Williams</a> led World War II raid on the <a href="/wiki/Schweinfurt%E2%80%93Regensburg_mission" title="Schweinfurt?Regensburg mission">Schweinfurt ball bearing factories</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AFLink_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFLink-230"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup> General <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Adolph_Schriever" title="Bernard Adolph Schriever">Bernard Adolph Schriever</a>, known as &quot;the architect of the Air Force?s ballistic missile and military space program&quot;, became the namesake of <a href="/wiki/Schriever_Air_Force_Base" title="Schriever Air Force Base">Schriever Air Force Base</a>, Colorado.<sup id="cite_ref-Schriever_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schriever-231"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Schviever2_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schviever2-232"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup> General <a href="/wiki/T._Michael_Moseley" title="T. Michael Moseley">Michael Moseley</a> is a former Chief of Staff of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">United States Air Force</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Moseley_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moseley-233"><span>[</span>230<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In addition, seven Aggies received the <a href="/wiki/Medal_of_Honor" title="Medal of Honor">Medal of Honor</a> in World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-medalofhonor_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-medalofhonor-234"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup> The recipients are:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Horace_S._Carswell,_Jr." title="Horace S. Carswell, Jr.">Horace S. Carswell, Jr., class of 1938</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Thomas_W._Fowler" title="Thomas W. Fowler">Thomas W. Fowler, class of 1943</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/William_Harrell" title="William Harrell" class="mw-redirect">William G. Harrell, class of 1943</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Lloyd_H._Hughes" title="Lloyd H. Hughes" class="mw-redirect">Lloyd H. Hughes, class of 1943</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/George_Keathley" title="George Keathley" class="mw-redirect">George D. Keathley, class of 1937</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Turney_W._Leonard" title="Turney W. Leonard">Turney W. Leonard, class of 1942</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Eli_L._Whiteley" title="Eli L. Whiteley">Eli L. Whiteley, class of 1941</a> 
       <div style="clear:both;"></div> </li> 
     </ul> 
     <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_A%26M_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;"> 
      <ol class="references"> 
       <li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Note that the seal contains the date 1876, the year in which Texas A&amp;M began classes. This is not a discrepancy as both 1871 (the year the Texas Legislature appropriated funds to begin A&amp;M's construction) and 1876 can be considered the dates of establishment depending on the definition used and the reference sourced (even within the Texas A&amp;M University system).</span></li> 
       <li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The institution's branch campuses, <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_University_at_Galveston" title="Texas A&amp;M University at Galveston">Texas A&amp;M University at Galveston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_University_at_Qatar" title="Texas A&amp;M University at Qatar">Texas A&amp;M University at Qatar</a>, are considered part of Texas A&amp;M proper. These are in <a href="/wiki/Galveston,_Texas" title="Galveston, Texas">Galveston, Texas</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Education_City" title="Education City">Education City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">Doha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a> respectively.</span></li> 
       <li id="cite_note-73"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-73">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In the <i>U.S. News and World Report</i> ranking, Texas A&amp;M tied with <a href="/wiki/Purdue_University" title="Purdue University">Purdue University</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Worcester_Polytechnic_Institute" title="Worcester Polytechnic Institute">Worcester Polytechnic Institute</a>.</span></li> 
      </ol> 
     </div>
